The Absolute Proposition: Actual Affirmation
Commentary expands on the absolute proposition and its relation to modalities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core meaning of a proposition as actual affirmation and distinguish it from modal qualifications.

Core Idea
Every proposition, even a false one, asserts actual affirmation of a predicate.

This passage tackles a subtle point: even an impossible proposition like 'Zayd is a stone' contains an underlying actual affirmation. The glossator and commentator unpack how the absolute proposition (al-qadiyya al-mutlaqa) is defined as pure affirmation before any modality is added. Understanding this helps clarify the structure of modal propositions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the counterexample
The glossator mentions that some minds hesitate at the example 'Zayd is a stone' (impossible). Note that this is presented as a challenge to the view that all propositions involve affirmation.
The example is deliberately impossible to test the definition.
2
Recognize the role of modality
The word 'by impossibility' (bil-imtina‘) qualifies the underlying assertion. The modality indicates that the affirmation is false in reality, but the affirmation itself is still present as the core of the proposition.
Modalities like necessity, possibility, impossibility are additions to the base affirmation.
3
Understand the absolute proposition
The commentator defines the absolute proposition as actual affirmation (al-thubut al-fi‘li). This is the basic meaning before any modal restriction. It is the foundation upon which modalities are built.
Actual affirmation is the common element in all propositions, true or false.
4
Distinguish between absolute and restricted
The absolute proposition is more general than any modalized proposition. Assent to a restricted proposition (e.g., with impossibility) includes assent to the absolute, but not vice versa. The absolute does not depend on the truth of the restricted.
This distinction is crucial for logical analysis of modal statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «الحاشية»: رب ذهن يتوقف في نحو قولنا «زيد حجر» بالامتناع ، بل يورده نقضا على ما ذكرنا لكن دقيق الفهم يفهم أن المفقود قبل ذكر الامتناع هو اعتقاد الوقوع واللاوقوع ، وإلا فأي شيء يوصف بالامتناع، فتعقل فإنه دقيق. الحاصل أن أصل النسبة عبارة عن مطلق الثبوت أعم من أن يكون بالفعل أو بالقوة أو بالضرورة أو بالامتناع ، وذا موجود في ضمن «زيد حجر بالامتناع» و«الحمار مركوب زيد (بالإمكان ومذعن أيضا في ضمن إذعانه، فلم يتخلف المطلق عن المقيد، ولا إذعانه عن إذعانه ، وإنما المفقود في زيد حجر بالامتناع الإذعان بالمعنى المتبادر عن مطلقه . قال بعض الشارحين : الضرورة قاضية بأن معنى مطلق القضية الثبوت الفعلي، وهو يوصف تارة بالضرورة، وتارة بالإمكان وتارة بالامتناع ، كيف ، ليس الممتنع مثلا إلا تحقق الثبوت في نفس الأمر ، وليس الفعلية زائدة عليه، ومن المتقرر أن الامتناع جهة القضية الكاذبة والثبوت المطلق صادق كما عرفت، ولو كان مدلول القضية أعم من الامتناع لما كان محتملا للصدق والكذب، واعتراف هذا بعيد عن الإنصاف . فالحق أن مدلول القضية هو الثبوت الفعلي، وهو قد يلاحظ ويقيد بالامتناع والضرورة والدوام والإمكان ، لكن تحقق بعض منها لا يقتضي تحقق المطلق، بل رفعه وسلبه والإذعان بالمقيد لا يستلزم الإذعان بالمطلق، وصدقه لا يتوقف على صدقه ؛ فإن الامتناع لا يتكيف به إلا ما هو باطل ، اهـ . وإني لا أفقه حق التفقه ؛ فإنه إذا قيل زيد (حجر وأريد معنى أعم يفيد فائدة تامة البتة، وليس إنشاء ، فهو خبر ،فمعنى القضية الثبوت المطلق، سواء كان على نهج الضرورة أو الإمكان أو الامتناع ، وهو المقيد بقيد الامتناع، وما
He said in the gloss: Many minds hesitate about our saying 'Zayd is a stone' by impossibility, and even present it as a counterexample to what we mentioned, but one of subtle understanding understands that what is missing before the mention of impossibility is the belief of occurrence and non-occurrence; otherwise, what could be described as impossible? So ponder, for it is subtle. The conclusion is that the basis of the relative predicate is absolute affirmation, whether actual or potential or necessary or impossible, and that is present within 'Zayd is a stone by impossibility' and 'the donkey is a mount of Zayd by possibility', and it is also assented to within his assent; so the absolute does not lag behind the restricted, nor its assent behind its assent. Rather, what is missing in 'Zayd is a stone by impossibility' is the assent in the primary sense of its absolute. Some commentators said: Necessity dictates that the meaning of the absolute proposition is actual affirmation, which is described sometimes by necessity, sometimes by possibility, and sometimes by impossibility. How so? For the impossible, for example, is nothing but the realization of affirmation in reality, and actuality is not additional to it. And it is established that impossibility is the modality of the false proposition and absolute affirmation is true, as you know. If the signification of the proposition were more general than impossibility, it would not be liable to truth and falsity. And this acknowledgment is far from fairness. The truth is that the signification of the proposition is actual affirmation, which may be observed and restricted by impossibility, necessity, perpetuity, and possibility. But the realization of some of these does not necessitate the realization of the absolute; rather, its raising and negation. And assent to the restricted does not entail assent to the absolute, and its truth does not depend on its truth; for impossibility only qualifies what is false. End. And I do not fully comprehend; for when it is said 'Zayd is a stone' and a more general meaning is intended, it surely gives a complete benefit, and it is not a construction, it is a report. So the meaning of the proposition is absolute affirmation, whether it is in the manner of necessity, possibility, or impossibility, and it is restricted by the restriction of impossibility.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from a glossator and another commentator on the nature of absolute propositions and their modalities. The glossator addresses a counterexample: if one says 'Zayd is a stone' (which is impossible), some might object that this statement does not involve any actual affirmation. The subtle point is that before considering the modality of impossibility, the statement is understood as a claim of actual affirmation (thubut fi‘li), but the modality of impossibility indicates that this affirmation is false in reality. The glossator concludes that the basis of any relative predicate is absolute affirmation, encompassing actual, potential, necessary, or impossible. This absolute affirmation is present even in an impossible proposition like 'Zayd is a stone' because the proposition still predicates something of Zayd, even if false. The assent (tasdiq) to the absolute is also present in the assent to the restricted. Then the commentator (Hamd Allah al-Sindili) argues that the meaning of the absolute proposition is actual affirmation (al-thubut al-fi‘li), which then can be qualified by modalities. He warns that if the proposition's signification were more general than impossibility, it could not be false, because absolute affirmation is always true. Therefore, the truth is that the proposition signifies actual affirmation, which can be restricted by modalities. The author of Bahr Ulum then adds his own confusion: he questions how 'Zayd is a stone' can be considered a report (khabar) with a complete benefit, and suggests that the meaning of the proposition is absolute affirmation regardless of modality. The passage uses the example of an impossible statement to illustrate the relationship between absolute affirmation and modal qualifications.

Distinguishing Absolute and Modal Propositions
Author clarifies absolute vs modal propositions and the weakness of possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between absolute (mutlaqa) and modal (muwajjaha) propositions and explain why possibility is the weakest modality.

Core Idea
Absolute is the default; modal adds a modality; possibility is unstable.

In this passage, the author clarifies a foundational distinction in logic: the difference between an absolute proposition—which simply reports without qualification—and a modal proposition, which includes a necessity, impossibility, or possibility. Understanding this distinction is essential for evaluating the strength of claims in Islamic sciences, where modalities often determine the certainty of a judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposition types
Find where the author distinguishes absolute (mutlaqa) from modal (muwajjaha). Note that absolute propositions judge only the common understanding without additional modality, while modal propositions include a modality like necessity, impossibility, or possibility.
The author states that the convention is to call a proposition 'absolute' if it judges only the common understanding when unqualified, and 'modal' if it judges an additional aspect.
2
Understand the weakness of possibility
Locate where the author discusses possibility (imkan). He describes it as the weakest mode because it indicates instability—the connection may or may not be. Contrast this with necessity (wujub) and impossibility (imtina'), which indicate a firm connection.
The author says possibility is 'tazalzul' (unstable), while necessity and impossibility are 'wathiqat al-ribat' (firm connection).
3
Analyze the relationship between absolute and modal
Examine the author's argument that a true qualified (modal) proposition implies the truth of the absolute form. He uses the analogy of part and whole: the truth of the specific entails the truth of the general.
The author argues that allowing the truth of a qualified proposition with the falsehood of the absolute would be like separating a part from the whole.
4
Apply the distinction to Islamic science examples
Take a statement like 'The world is originated' (absolute) and compare it to 'The world is necessarily originated' (modal necessity). Recognize that the absolute is the default, and the modal adds a claim about the mode of connection.
This distinction is crucial in kalam when discussing divine attributes: some are necessary, some possible, some impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكملة لمباحث الموجهات هو متقرر ليس إلا بمعنى أن ما هو كاذب بالمعنى المتبادر موجهة بجهة الامتناع وليس القضية محتملة للصدق والكذب إلا بمعنى أن نفس مفهومه من حيث إنه حكاية عن شيء، ومحتمل للمطابقة وعدمها، وهو حاصل في المطلق الأعم، وأما امتناع كذبه فلا ينافي كونه قضية وخبرا، بل يؤكده. وتجويز صدق المقيد مع كذب المطلق تجويز انسلاخ الجزء عن الكل، وتحقق الأخص من دون تحقق الأعم، بل الضرورة تقتضي أن صدق المقيد بعينه صدق المطلق، وتجويز تقييد شيء بما ينافيه تجويز اجتماع المتنافيين. هذا كله ظاهر عند من له أدنى عقل وإنصاف. هذا، والله أعلم بالصواب. نعم، ذلك، أي الثبوت بالإمكان أضعف المدارح؛ لتزلزله بين أن لا يكون، ومن ثم قالوا الوجوب والامتناع دالة، والأظهر دالان على وثاقة الرابط؛ لدلالة الأول على وقوع الربط جزما، والثاني على عدم وقوعه جزما، والإمكان على ضعفها؛ لدلالته على التزلزل، فالثبوت بطريق الإمكان نحو من الثبوت مطلقا، الذي هو مدلول مطلق القضية. غاية الأمر المتبادر منه، أي مما دل على الثبوت عند الإطلاق، أي لفظ عند عدم تقييده بالجهات هو الوقوع على نسج الفعلية؛ لعدم وضع في لغة للثبوت المطلق، وذلك المتبادر لا يضر في عمومه، كما قالوا في الوجود إنه مطلق التحقق، وإن كان المتبادر التحقق في الخارج، وإذا كانت موجهة فالمطلقة العامة بالطريق الأولى. فيه أنه لا يلزم من كون الممكنة موجهة كون المطلقة موجهة لا لأن مفاد مطلق القضية الثبوت الفعلي؛ لما عرفت، بل لأن الاصطلاح وقع على أن القضية التي حكم فيها بما يتبادر عند الإطلاق فحسب مطلقة، وإن حكم فيها على أمر زائد فموجهة. ولعل السر فيه أن مطلق القضية الدالة على الثبوت مطلقا لا يتعلق بها غرض علمي، فلم يبحث عنها ولم يسم والغرض إنما يتعلق بما يدل على المعنى المتبادر، أو على ما يزيد فسمي الأول مطلقة والثاني موجهة. هذا ما يحكم به الفحص البالغ في كلمات المتقدمين ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمرا.
Continuation of discussions on modal propositions. It is settled only in the sense that what is false in the common understanding is modal with the modality of impossibility, and the proposition is not possible of truth and falsehood except in the sense that its very concept, insofar as it is a report about something, is possible of correspondence and non-correspondence, and this is found in the absolute general. As for the impossibility of its falsehood, it does not contradict its being a proposition and a statement; rather it confirms it. And allowing the truth of the qualified along with the falsehood of the absolute is allowing the separation of the part from the whole, and the existence of the more specific without the existence of the more general; rather necessity requires that the truth of the qualified is precisely the truth of the absolute. And allowing the qualification of something with what contradicts it is allowing the conjunction of two contradictory things. All this is clear to anyone with minimal reason and fairness. This, and God knows best what is correct. Yes, that, i.e., affirmation by possibility, is the weakest of modes; because of its instability between being and not being. And hence they said: necessity and impossibility indicate, and the more apparent is they both indicate the firmness of the connection; because the first indicates the occurrence of the connection definitely, and the second indicates its non-occurrence definitely, and possibility indicates its weakness; because it indicates instability. So affirmation by way of possibility is a kind of affirmation absolutely, which is the signification of the absolute proposition. The ultimate matter: the common understanding from it, i.e., from what indicates affirmation when unqualified, i.e., the word when not qualified by modalities, is occurrence in the manner of actuality; because there is no lexical convention for absolute affirmation. And that common understanding does not harm its generality, as they said regarding existence: it is absolute realization, even if the common understanding is realization in the external. And if it is modal, then the general absolute is a fortiori. In it: It does not follow from the possible being modal that the absolute is modal, not because the import of the absolute proposition is actual affirmation, as you knew, but because the convention settled that the proposition in which what is commonly understood when unqualified is judged is only absolute, and if it is judged regarding an additional aspect, it is modal. Perhaps the secret in this is that the absolute proposition indicating affirmation absolutely has no scientific purpose attached to it, so it was not investigated and not named; rather the purpose is attached to what indicates the common understanding, or what is additional; so the first was called absolute and the second modal. This is what thorough investigation of the words of the predecessors dictates, and perhaps God will produce afterwards a matter.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and clarificatory continuation of the discussion on modal propositions. The author begins by emphasizing that a proposition that is false in the common understanding is modal with the modality of impossibility, but this does not negate its being a proposition; it actually confirms it because falsity presupposes a claim about reality. He then addresses the ability to conceive of a qualified (e.g., particular) proposition being true while the absolute (general) form is false, arguing this is impossible because the truth of the qualified entails the truth of the absolute, like a part cannot exist without the whole. Allowing such would allow contradictions. Next, he reiterates that affirmation by possibility (imkan) is the weakest mode because it is unstable, unlike necessity and impossibility which indicate a firm connection positively or negatively. He clarifies that 'absolute' in common usage means actual occurrence (wuqu' fi'li), but this does not limit the generality of the term; it can still apply to mental existence. When a proposition is modal, the absolute is still primary. He explains that the convention is to call propositions that only express the common understanding 'absolute', and those that add a modality 'modal', because the plain absolute has no scientific utility. The passage ends with reliance on the predecessors' insights.

Indicators of Non-Permanence and Non-Necessity
Author explains that 'non-permanent' and 'non-necessary' indicate general absolute and general possible propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the terms 'non-permanence' and 'non-necessity' function as indicators of proposition types and explain why they imply rather than directly express judgments.

Core Idea
Non-permanence and non-necessity 'remove' modes of the relation, pointing to opposite propositions by implicit indication.

In this lesson, we explore two key technical terms from modal logic: 'non-permanence' (al-ladawam) and 'non-necessity' (al-ladarura). The author explains that these terms serve as indicators for specific types of propositions. Understanding their function is essential for parsing compound logical statements correctly. We'll break down how they operate as 'removers' and why they indicate implied judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms and their opposites
Locate 'al-ladawam' and 'al-ladarura' in the text. Note that they are opposites to permanence and necessity.
2
Understand their function as removers (rafi'an)
The author says they remove the relation of permanence and necessity. This means they negate those modes.
3
Connect to the type of proposition indicated
Al-ladawam indicates a general absolute proposition (mutlaqa 'amma), while al-ladarura indicates a general possible proposition (mumkina 'amma). Explain why: removal of permanence yields absolute; removal of necessity yields possible.
4
Recognize implicit indication (dalil iltizami)
The terms do not directly express propositions but imply them. The singular term does not match a full sentence, so the composite proposition is actually multiple.
5
Apply the criterion of unity of judgment
Understand why a composite proposition is considered multiple: because unity of judgment depends on quality, subject, predicate. Here quality differs, so it is multiple.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الخامس: اللادوام إشارة إلى مطلقة عامة، واللاضرورة إشارة إلى ممكنة عامة، حال كونهما مخالفتي الكيفية وموافقتى الكمية لما قيد بهما، هو الأصل؛ لأنهما رافعان للنسبة من حيث دوامها وضرورتها، فيلزم فعلية ما يناقضها أو إمكانها من غير تفاوت في الرفع. وفيه إشارة إلى أنهما سواء في الدلالة على القضية المخالفة؛ فإنهما دالان التزاما؛ إذ المفرد لا يدل على الجملة مطابقة، فالمركبة قضية متعددة؛ لأن العبرة في وحدتها وتعددها بوحدة الحكم وتعدده، وتعدده إما باختلافه كيفا أو موضوعا أو محمولا، لا رابع لها، والأول موجود ههنا، فوجب التعدد.
The fifth investigation: Non-permanence is an indication of a general absolute [proposition], and non-necessity is an indication of a general possible [proposition], both being opposite in quality and matching in quantity to what they qualify. This is the principle; because they both remove the relation from the perspective of its permanence and necessity, so the actuality of what contradicts it or its possibility follows, without differentiation in removal. In it is an indication that they are equal in indicating the opposite proposition; for they both indicate implicitly; since the singular does not indicate the sentence explicitly, so the composite is a multiple proposition; because the criterion for its unity and multiplicity is the unity and multiplicity of the judgment, and its multiplicity is either by its difference in quality, or subject, or predicate, with no fourth, and the first is present here, so multiplicity is necessary.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and analytical section establishing the function of the terms 'non-permanence' (al-ladawam) and 'non-necessity' (al-ladarura) as indicators of proposition types. The author states that 'non-permanence' indicates a general absolute proposition, and 'non-necessity' indicates a general possible proposition. These two terms are opposite in quality (they negate permanence/necessity) but match in quantity (they apply to the same subject as the original proposition). The core idea is that they are 'removers' (rafi'an) of the relation from the aspect of its permanence and necessity. Consequently, either the actuality of the opposite (i.e., the contradictory) or the possibility of the opposite follows, without any difference in the removal operation. The author then notes that these two indicators are equivalent in their implicit reference to the opposite proposition; they are 'dalil iltizami' (implicit indications) because a singular term does not directly express a full proposition. Finally, he argues that a composite proposition (e.g., a conditional or modal statement) is actually multiple propositions because the criterion for unity is the unity of the judgment. Multiplicity occurs through difference in quality, subject, or predicate. Since here there is a difference in quality (negation of permanence), the proposition is multiple.

D) It affirms permanence.

Key Takeaway
Non-permanence and non-necessity are implicit indicators that remove modes from the relation, thereby pointing to opposite proposition types.

The Four Relations in Propositions: Truth-Based Equivalence and Entailment
Author explains that the four relations apply to propositions based on actual truth, not predication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between equality (mutasawiyatan) and entailment (talazum) in propositions based on their truth values, and explain why the four relations in propositions are based on actual truth rather than predication.

Core Idea
Proposition relations are measured by truth, not predication.

We are used to thinking of the four relations (equality, entailment, contrast, disparity) as applying to terms based on predication. But what about whole propositions? The author clarifies that propositions cannot be predicated of each other, so their relations are defined by their truth in reality. This shift is essential for understanding how statements in Kalam or Fiqh relate logically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shift from terms to propositions
Notice that for singular terms (mufradat), the four relations are based on predication (haml). For propositions (qadaya), predication is impossible because propositions are not predicates. The author explicitly says: 'la tuhmalu la ala al-qadaya wa la ala al-mufradat'.
This is a fundamental point: the unit of analysis changes from terms to truth.
2
Define the basis: truth in reality (sidq fi al-waqi')
The relations among propositions are 'bi hasbi sidqiha fi al-waqi''—according to their actual truth. This means truth values (true/false) form the foundation, not predicative structure.
3
Understand equality (mutasawiyatan)
Two propositions are equal when they are always both true or both false. That is, their truth values are perfectly correlated. The author says: 'allatani talazamata fi al-sidq mutasawiyatan'.
In term logic, equality meant 'every A is B and every B is A'. Here it means 'true together, false together'.
4
Understand entailment (talazum)
Entailment means the truth of one proposition requires the truth of the other. The author begins to describe it: 'allatani talazum sidq ahadeehma...' (the two that require the truth of one of them). The reverse may not hold.
This corresponds to implication in modern logic, but note it's a relation between propositions, not conditionals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السادس: النسب الأربع في المفردات بحسب الصدق على شيء، وفي القضايا لا يتصور ذلك؛ لأنها لا تحمل لا على القضايا ولا على المفردات، وإنما هي، أي النسب فيه بحسب صدقها في الواقع، فاللتان تلازمتا في الصدق متساويتان، واللتان تلازم صدق أحدهما
The sixth investigation: The four relations in singular terms are according to predication on something, but in propositions this is not conceivable; because propositions are not predicated of propositions nor of singular terms. Rather, they, i.e., the relations [in propositions] are according to their truth in reality. So the two that are concomitant in truth are equal, and the two that require the truth of one of them...
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage, though truncated, establishes a key principle: the four relations (nisab arba')—which are typically discussed for terms (equal, convertible, etc.) based on predication—apply differently to propositions. For propositions, the relations are not based on predication (since propositions are not predicated of each other) but are based on their actual truth values in reality. The author begins to enumerate: if two propositions are always true together, they are equivalent. If the truth of one necessitates the truth of the other, it is entailment. The text breaks off before completing the four types, but the essential point is that the truth-based relations for propositions mirror the predication-based relations for terms.

Key Terms
النسب الأربع
صدق
متساويتان
تلازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis are the four relations applied to propositions according to this passage?
A) Predication of one proposition on another.
B) The truth of the propositions in reality.
C) The quantity and quality of the propositions.
D) The modality of the propositions.

Key Takeaway
The four relations among propositions are determined by their truth values, not by predication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Ladawam and Ladharura: Indication by Implication
Defines al-ladawam and al-ladharura and explains multiplicity of compound propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how ladawam and ladharura indicate general modals by implication and identify why compound propositions become multiple in judgment.

Core Idea
Ladawam and ladharura indicate modals by removal, not by direct naming.

This passage clarifies two key modal terms in Islamic logic. Unlike simple modal propositions, ladawam and ladharura do not directly name their corresponding propositions; they indicate them through implication (iltizam). Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly analyzing compound modal propositions and recognizing when a proposition is multiple due to a change in judgment.

Guided Path
1
Define the key modal terms
Identify the literal meanings and what each term indicates: ladawam (non-perpetuity) indicates the general absolute proposition (mutilaqa 'amma), and ladharura (non-necessity) indicates the general possible proposition (mumkina 'amma).
Remember that these terms are not themselves propositions but single terms that imply whole propositions.
2
Understand the mode of indication
Note that the author stresses they indicate by implication (iltizam) not by conformity (mutabaqa). A single term cannot directly signify a full proposition; it implies the existence of the relation being negated.
The terms are 'removers' (rafi'an) of perpetuity or necessity, so they point to the contradictory or the possibility of the original relation.
3
Analyze the compound proposition
When these terms are combined with a base proposition (e.g., 'Zakat is not perpetual'), the resulting compound is considered a single or multiple proposition based on the judgment.
The criterion for unity/multiplicity is the judgment itself: if the judgment changes in quality, subject, or predicate, the proposition is multiple.
4
Apply the multiplicity criterion
In this case, the judgment changes in quality (negation of perpetuity/necessity), so the compound proposition is necessarily multiple. There is no fourth way for judgment to vary.
This means that 'Zakat is perpetual' and 'Zakat is not perpetual' are two distinct propositions, not a single compound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث (الْخَامِسُ : اللَّادَوَامُ إِشَارَةٌ إِلى مُطْلَقَةٍ عَامَّةٍ، وَاللَّاضَرُورَةُ) إشارة (إِلَى مُمْكِنَةٍ عَامَّةٍ)، حال كونهما (مُخَالِفَتَيْ الْكَيْفِيَّةِ وَمُوَافِقَتَيْ الْكَمِّيَّةِ لِمَا قُيِّدَ بهما)، هو الأصل؛ لِأَنَّهُمَا رَافِعَانِ لِلنِّسْبَةِ، من حيث دوامها وضرورتها، فيلزم فعلية ما يناقضها أو إمكانها مِنْ غَيْرِ تَفَاوُتٍ في الرفع. وفيه إشارة إلى أنهما سواء في الدلالة على القضية المخالفة؛ فإنهما دالان التزاما؛ إذ المفرد لا يدل على الجملة مطابقة، (فَالْمُرَكَّبَةُ قَضِيَّةٌ مُتَعَدِّدَةٌ؛ لِأَنَّ الْعِبْرَةَ فِي وَحْدَتِهَا وَتَعَدُّدُهَا بِوَحْدَةِ الْحُكُم وَتَعَدُدِهِ، وَتَعَدُدُهُ إِمَّا بِاخْتِلَافِهِ كَيْفًا أَوْ مَوْضُوعًا أَوْ مَحْمُولًا، لَا رَابِعَ لَهَا)، والأول موجود ههنا، فوجب التعدد.
The fifth investigation: al-ladawam (non-perpetuity) is an indication to the general absolute, and al-ladharura (non-necessity) is an indication to the general possible, while they are both contrary in quality and agreeing in quantity to what they are restricted to; that is the principle because they are removers of the relation from the aspect of its perpetuity and necessity, so the actuality of its contradictory or its possibility follows without disparity in removal. And in it is an indication that they are equal in indication of the contrary proposition; for they indicate by implication, since a single term does not indicate the sentence by conformity. So the compound proposition is multiple, because the consideration in its unity and multiplicity is with the unity or multiplicity of the judgment, and its multiplicity is either by its difference in quality, subject, or predicate, with no fourth. And the first exists here, so multiplicity is necessary.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage explains that the terms 'al-ladawam' (non-perpetuity) and 'al-ladharura' (non-necessity) do not directly name a type of modal proposition but rather indicate the general absolute and general possible propositions by implication. They are 'removers' (rafi'an) of the relation's perpetuity or necessity, implying the contradictory or possibility of that relation. The author stresses that these terms indicate the contrary proposition only by implication, not by direct conformity (mutabaqa). This leads to the conclusion that a compound proposition—one formed by such a term plus the original proposition—is actually multiple in terms of judgment, because the judgment differs (in quality or quantity). For example, the statement 'it is not perpetual' changes the judgment of the original proposition, making it a distinct proposition. The unifying factor is the judgment itself; if the judgment changes, the proposition is multiple. Here, because the judgment differs in quality (negation of perpetuity/necessity), the compound is considered multiple.

Key Terms
اللادوام (al-ladawam): A term (literally 'non-perpetuity') used to indicate a general absolute proposition (مطلقة عامة) by negating the perpetuity of the relation. [Note: No significant shift.]
اللاضرورة (al-ladharura): A term (literally 'non-necessity') used to indicate a general possible proposition (ممكنة عامة) by negating the necessity of the relation. [Note: No significant shift.]
القضية المركبة (al-qadiyya al-murakkaba): A proposition formed by combining a term (like ladawam) with another proposition; here argued to be multiple due to a change in judgment. [Note: In later works, 'compound proposition' may refer to conditional or disjunctive propositions, but here it is specifically about modal compounds.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a compound proposition formed with ladawam considered multiple?
A) Because the subject changes
B) Because the judgment differs in quality
C) Because the predicate changes
D) Because it contains two terms

Key Takeaway
Ladawam and ladharura indicate general absolute and possible propositions by implication, and when combined with a base proposition they produce a multiplicity of judgments because the judgment changes in quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the phrase 'al-salat la tadum' (prayer is not perpetual). Determine which modal proposition this implies (general absolute or general possible) and explain why the compound 'prayer is not perpetual' is a separate proposition from 'prayer is perpetual'.
?
In a kalam argument, a mutakallim says 'The world is not necessary (la darura)'. Identify the implied modal proposition and show that this compound proposition counts as multiple because the judgment changes from necessity to non-necessity.

Initial Concepts vs. Philosophical Principles in Modal Relations
Methodology: initial concepts vs. philosophical principles in modal relations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the initial-conceptual (badi' al-ra'y) and philosophical perspectives in determining relations among modal propositions, and identify the relation between the necessary absolute and perpetual absolute from each perspective.

Core Idea
Logic judges modal relations by immediate concepts, not by philosophical proofs about chance.

This passage establishes a foundational methodological principle for modal logic: the relations among different types of propositions (necessary, perpetual, possible) are determined by our immediate conceptual understanding, not by deep philosophical principles. The author illustrates this with the relation between the necessary absolute (al-ḍarūriyya al-muṭlaqa) and the perpetual absolute (al-dā'ima al-muṭlaqa), which differs depending on whether you adopt the initial perspective or a philosophical one. Understanding this distinction enables you to correctly extract the relationships among all modal propositions without importing controversial doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two perspectives
The passage contrasts 'badi' al-ra'y' (initial immediate understanding) with 'al-uṣūl al-daqīqa allatī burhina ʿalayhā fī al-falsafa' (precise principles proven in philosophy). Logic should be built on the former, not the latter.
The author explicitly says it is not fitting to build issues of this art (logic) on philosophical issues.
2
Examine the example: necessary vs. perpetual
According to initial understanding, every necessary proposition is perpetual (continuous truth as long as the subject exists), but not vice versa because perpetuity could happen by chance. Hence the necessary absolute is absolutely more specific (akhaṣṣ muṭlaqan) than the perpetual absolute.
For example, 'Every human is animal' is necessary; 'Every raven is black' might be perpetual by chance, not necessary.
3
Switch to the philosophical perspective
If one relies on philosophical proofs that deny chance (al-bakht) and accident (al-ittifāq), then perpetuity implies necessity, making the two equivalent.
The passage notes that on the philosophical view, 'a thing does not perpetually exist without necessity.'
4
Apply the principle to extract other relations
The author then uses initial concepts to judge that the general possible (al-mumkina al-ʿāmma) is the most general of all propositions. The passage also mentions the particular possible (al-mumkina al-khāṣṣa) as the most general among compound modalities.
This is based on the idea that possibility can coexist with non-necessity and non-perpetuity, whereas necessity and perpetuity cannot coexist with their opposites.
5
Check the grounding of logical relations
The principle ensures that logic remains independent of controversial philosophical doctrines. Modal relations are determined by what we immediately understand, keeping logic universally accessible.
This is relevant for Islamic sciences that rely on logical reasoning without committing to specific philosophical positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْمَنْظُورُ فِي النِّسْبَةِ مَا يُحْكَمُ بِهِ مَفْهُومَاتُهَا فِي بَادِئِ الرَّأْيِ، من غير ملاحظة مقدمات فلسفية، (أَمَّا بِنَاءُ الْكَلَامِ عَلَى الْأُصولِ الدَّقِيقَةِ الَّتِي بُرْهِنَ عَلَيْهَا فى الْفَلْسَفَةِ)، كبطلان البخت والاتفاق، فَذَلِكَ مَرْتَبَةٌ بَعْدَ تَحْصِيل هَذَا الْفَنّ) (۱)) ، فلا يليق بناء مسائل هذا الفن على مسائلها . (وَمِنْ ثَمَّ)، أي من أجل أن المنظور حكم المفهومات في بادئ الرأي (قَالُوا : إِنَّ الضَّرُورِيَّةَ الْمُطْلَقَةَ أَخَصُّ مُطْلَقًا مِنَ الدَّائِمَةِ الْمُطْلَقَةِ)؛ فإن كل ما كان ضروريا لشيء ما دام الذات كان دائما كذلك من غير عكس؛ لجواز الدوام بالاتفاق من غير وجوب، أما لو بني على ما برهن في الفلسفة فهما متساويتان؛ فإن الشيء لا يدوم، بل لا يوجد من غير وجوب بالبخت والاتفاق. ( وَحِينَئِذٍ لَا يُسْتَصْعَبُ عَلَيْكَ اسْتِخْرَاجُ النَّسَبِ بَيْنَ الْمُوَجَّهَاتِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ ، وَلَوِ اسْتَقْرَيْتَ) حال الموجهات عَلِمْتَ أَنَّ الْمُمْكِنَةَ الْعَامَّةَ أَعَمُّ الْقَضَايَا) كلها، بسائط كانت أو مركبة؛ فإن ضرورة النسبة مطلقا ودوامها مطلقا وفعليتها مطلقا لا تجامع مع ضرورة مقابلها، وأما إمكان النسبة فقد يوجد من غير ضرورة ودوام وفعلية. وأما بناء على الأصول الدقيقة فالممكنة الميزانية والمطلقة العامة متساويتان؛ لأن نقيضي المتساويين متساويان . (وَالْمُمْكِنَةُ الْخَاصَّةُ أَعَمُّ الْمُرَكَّبَاتِ)؛ فإن تحقق النسبة من غير ضرورة أو دوام، بل وقوع مقابلها في حين من الأحيان مستلزم لتساوي الطرفين من غير
Then the perspective in the relation is what is judged by its concepts at first glance, without consideration of philosophical premises. As for building the discourse upon the precise principles that are proven in philosophy, like the invalidity of chance and accident, that is a rank after mastering this art, so it is not fitting to build the issues of this art upon its issues. And from that, i.e., because the perspective is the judgment of concepts at first glance, they said: The necessary absolute is absolutely more specific than the perpetual absolute; for everything that is necessary for a thing as long as the essence exists is perpetual likewise without converse, because of the possibility of perpetuity by chance without necessity. As for if it were built upon what is proven in philosophy, they would be equivalent, for a thing does not perpetually exist, rather does not exist without necessity by chance and accident. And then it will not be difficult for you to extract the relations among the mentioned modalities, and if you investigate the state of the modalities, you will know that the general possible is the most general of all propositions, simple or compound, for the necessity of the relation absolutely and its perpetuity absolutely and its actuality absolutely do not coexist with the necessity of its opposite. As for the possibility of the relation, it may exist without necessity, perpetuity, or actuality. And as for building upon the precise principles, the equally possible and the general absolute are equivalent, because the contradictories of equals are equal. And the particular possible is the most general of the compounds, for the actuality of the relation without necessity or perpetuity, rather the occurrence of its opposite at some time, necessitates the equality of the two sides without...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage sets a methodological principle: the relations among modalities in logic are based on immediate conceptual understanding (badi' al-ra'y), not on deep philosophical principles that prove things like the impossibility of chance (al-bakht) and accident (al-ittifaq). Logic should not borrow from philosophy. This directly affects how modal propositions are compared. For example, according to initial understanding, the 'necessary absolute' (al-daruriyya al-mutlaqa: a proposition that holds with necessity as long as the subject exists) is more specific than the 'perpetual absolute' (al-da'ima al-mutlaqa: a proposition that holds continuously, whether necessarily or by chance). The necessary implies perpetual, but not vice versa, because perpetual could happen by chance. However, if one uses philosophical proofs—which deny chance—they become equivalent. The author then applies this principle to extract relations among modalities: The 'general possible' (mumkina 'amma: not necessary nor perpetual) is the most general of all propositions, because it can accompany anything that is not necessary/perpetual. On the philosophical view, the 'balanced possible' (possible on both sides) equals the general absolute. The 'particular possible' (mumkina khassa: possible with a tendency) is the most general among compound modalities, because its condition (non-necessity and non-perpetuity, with occasional occurrence of the opposite) leads to equality of sides without requirement of necessity.

Key Terms
بادئ الرأي
الضَّرُورِيَّةُ الْمُطْلَقَةُ
الدائمَةُ الْمُطْلَقَةُ
المُمْكِنَةُ الْعَامَّةُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the initial conceptual perspective (بادئ الرأي), what is the relation between the necessary absolute and the perpetual absolute?
A) They are equivalent
B) The necessary absolute is absolutely more specific than the perpetual absolute
C) The perpetual absolute is more specific than the necessary absolute
D) They are disparate

Key Takeaway
Logic's modal relations are judged by immediate concepts, not by philosophical proofs; thus the necessary absolute is more specific than the perpetual absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the modal proposition: 'Every human is mortal.' According to initial concepts (badi' al-ra'y), is this proposition necessary absolute or perpetual absolute? Explain why, referring to the relation between the two modalities. Hint: think about the subject's existence.
?
If a philosopher proves that chance does not exist, how would the relation between necessary absolute and perpetual absolute change? Show the consequence for a proposition like 'Every raven is black' (assuming it happens to be always true by observation).
